(IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Welsh" title="Help:IPA/Welsh">[pla\xc9\xaad \xcb\x88k\xc9\x99mri]</a></span>; <span class="nowrap"><small>English:  </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\xcb\x8c</span><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">a\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span></span> <wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/\xca\x8c/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;cut&#39;">\xca\x8c</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> officially <b>Plaid Cymru \xe2\x80\x93 Party of Wales</b>, often referred to simply as <b>Plaid</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social-democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Wales" title="List of political parties in Wales">political party in Wales</a> advocating for <a href="/wiki/Welsh_independence" title="Welsh independence">Welsh independence</a> from the United Kingdom within the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Plaid was formed in 1925 and won its first seat in the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">UK Parliament</a> in 1966. By 2018, it held one of four Welsh seats in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, four of 40 Welsh seats in the UK Parliament, 10 of 60 seats in the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a>, and 202 of 1,264 principal local authority councillors.<sup id="cite_ref-Edkins_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edkins-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Plaid is a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Alliance" title="European Free Alliance">European Free Alliance</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="tocnumber">2.9.5</span> <span class="toctext">Fifth National Assembly, 2016\xe2\x80\x93present</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Undeb_Credyd_Plaid_Cymru"><span class="tocnumber">2.10</span> <span class="toctext">Undeb Credyd Plaid Cymru</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Party_leadership"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Party leadership</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Past_leaders"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Past leaders</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Deputy_leaders"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Deputy leaders</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Elected_representatives"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Elected representatives</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#UK_Parliament"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">UK Parliament</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#European_Parliament"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">European Parliament</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Local councillors</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Electoral_performance"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Electoral performance</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Local_elections"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Local elections</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#European_Parliament_elections"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">European Parliament elections</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#UK_general_elections"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">UK general elections</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#National_Assembly_for_Wales_elections"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">National Assembly for Wales elections</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#European_Free_Alliance"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">European Free Alliance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Platform">Platform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Platform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Plaid Cymru\'s goals as set out in its constitution are:\n</p>\n<ol><li>To promote the constitutional advancement of Wales with a view to attaining <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a> within the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>;</li>\n<li>To ensure economic prosperity, <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a> and the health of the natural environment, based on decentralist <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a>;</li>\n<li>To build a national community based on equal citizenship, respect for different traditions and cultures and the equal worth of all individuals, whatever their race, nationality, gender, colour, creed, sexuality, age, ability or social background;</li>\n<li>To create a <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">bilingual society</a> by promoting the revival of the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh language</a>;</li>\n<li>To promote Wales\'s contribution to the global community and to attain <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">membership of the</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.</li></ol>\n<p>In September 2008, a senior Plaid <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="Member of the National Assembly for Wales">assembly member</a> spelled out her party\'s continuing support for an independent Wales. The <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Rural_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister for Rural Affairs">Welsh Minister for Rural Affairs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elin_Jones" title="Elin Jones">Elin Jones</a>, began Plaid\'s annual conference by pledging to uphold the goal of making Wales a European Union member state. She told the delegates in <a href="/wiki/Aberystwyth" title="Aberystwyth">Aberystwyth</a> that the party would continue its commitment to independence under the coalition with the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Labour" title="Welsh Labour">Welsh Labour Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Plaid_Cymru" title="History of Plaid Cymru">History of Plaid Cymru</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings">Beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Penblwydd_Plaid_Cymru_Anniversary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_644944.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Penblwydd_Plaid_Cymru_Anniversary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_644944.jpg/220px-Penblwydd_Plaid_Cymru_Anniversary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_644944.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Penblwydd_Plaid_Cymru_Anniversary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_644944.jpg/330px-Penblwydd_Plaid_Cymru_Anniversary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_644944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Penblwydd_Plaid_Cymru_Anniversary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_644944.jpg/440px-Penblwydd_Plaid_Cymru_Anniversary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_644944.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="428" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Penblwydd_Plaid_Cymru_Anniversary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_644944.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plaque commemorating the founding of <span lang="cy" style="font-style:normal;" title="Welsh language text">Plaid Cymru, <a href="/wiki/Pwllheli" title="Pwllheli">Pwllheli</a></span></div></div></div>\n<p>While both the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal</a> parties of the early 20th century had accommodated demands for Welsh home rule, no political party existed for the purpose of establishing a Welsh government. <i lang="cy" title="Welsh language text">Plaid Genedlaethol Cymru</i> (English: <span lang="en">National Party of Wales</span>) was formed on 5 August 1925, by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moses_Gruffydd&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Moses Gruffydd (page does not exist)">Moses Gruffydd</a>, <a href="/wiki/H._R._Jones" class="mw-redirect" title="H. R. Jones">H. R. Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Valentine" title="Lewis Valentine">Lewis Valentine</a>, members of <i lang="cy" title="Welsh language text">Byddin Ymreolwyr Cymru</i> ("Home Rule Army of Wales"; literally, "Self-Rulers\' Army of Wales"); and Fred Jones, <a href="/wiki/Saunders_Lewis" title="Saunders Lewis">Saunders Lewis</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_John_Williams" title="David John Williams">David John Williams</a> of <i lang="cy" title="Welsh language text">Y Mudiad Cymreig</i> ("The Welsh Movement").<sup id="cite_ref-Ailgeni_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ailgeni-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Initially, home rule for Wales was not an explicit aim of the new movement; keeping Wales <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh-speaking</a> took primacy, with the aim of making Welsh the only official language of Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-Philip_1975_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philip_1975-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1929" title="United Kingdom general election, 1929">1929 general election</a> the party contested its first parliamentary constituency, <a href="/wiki/Caernarvonshire_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Caernarvonshire (UK Parliament constituency)">Caernarvonshire</a>, polling 609 votes, or 1.6% of the vote for that seat. The party contested few such elections in its early years, partly due to its ambivalence towards Westminster politics. Indeed, the candidate <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Valentine" title="Lewis Valentine">Lewis Valentine</a>, the party\xe2\x80\x99s first president, offered himself in Caernarvonshire on a platform of demonstrating Welsh people\'s rejection of English dominion.<sup id="cite_ref-McAllister_2001_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McAllister_2001-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1930s">1930s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1930s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>By 1932, the aims of <a href="/wiki/Self-government" class="mw-redirect" title="Self-government">self-government</a> and Welsh representation at the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> had been added to that of preserving Welsh language and culture. However, this move, and the party\'s early attempts to develop an economic critique, did not broaden its appeal beyond that of an intellectual and <a href="/wiki/Social_conservatism" title="Social conservatism">socially conservative</a> Welsh language pressure group.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The alleged sympathy of the party\'s leading members (including President <a href="/wiki/Saunders_Lewis" title="Saunders Lewis">Saunders Lewis</a>) towards Europe\'s <a href="/wiki/Totalitarianism" title="Totalitarianism">totalitarian regimes</a> compromised its early appeal further.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Saunders Lewis, David John Williams and Lewis Valentine attacked and set fire to the newly constructed RAF <a href="/wiki/Penyberth" title="Penyberth">Penyberth</a> air base on the <a href="/wiki/Ll%C5%B7n_Peninsula" title="Ll\xc5\xb7n Peninsula">Ll\xc5\xb7n Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gwynedd" title="Gwynedd">Gwynedd</a> in 1936, in protest at its siting in the Welsh-speaking heartland. The leaders\' treatment, including the trial judge\'s dismissal of the use of Welsh and their subsequent imprisonment in <a href="/wiki/Wormwood_Scrubs_(HM_Prison)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wormwood Scrubs (HM Prison)">Wormwood Scrubs</a>, led to "The Three" becoming a <i><a href="/wiki/Cause_c%C3%A9l%C3%A8bre" title="Cause c\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa8bre">cause c\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa8bre</a></i>. This heightened the profile of the party dramatically and its membership had doubled to nearly 2,000 by 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-Philip_1975_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philip_1975-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Y_tri_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Y_tri-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1940s">1940s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1940s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Plaid_Cymru_rally_in_Machynlleth_in_1949_where_the_%22Parliament_for_Wales_in_5_years%22_campaign_was_started_(14050400654).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/A_Plaid_Cymru_rally_in_Machynlleth_in_1949_where_the_%22Parliament_for_Wales_in_5_years%22_campaign_was_started_%2814050400654%29.jpg/220px-A_Plaid_Cymru_rally_in_Machynlleth_in_1949_where_the_%22Parliament_for_Wales_in_5_years%22_campaign_was_started_%2814050400654%29.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/A_Plaid_Cymru_rally_in_Machynlleth_in_1949_where_the_%22Parliament_for_Wales_in_5_years%22_campaign_was_started_%2814050400654%29.jpg/330px-A_Plaid_Cymru_rally_in_Machynlleth_in_1949_where_the_%22Parliament_for_Wales_in_5_years%22_campaign_was_started_%2814050400654%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/A_Plaid_Cymru_rally_in_Machynlleth_in_1949_where_the_%22Parliament_for_Wales_in_5_years%22_campaign_was_started_%2814050400654%29.jpg/440px-A_Plaid_Cymru_rally_in_Machynlleth_in_1949_where_the_%22Parliament_for_Wales_in_5_years%22_campaign_was_started_%2814050400654%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="586" data-file-height="404" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Plaid_Cymru_rally_in_Machynlleth_in_1949_where_the_%22Parliament_for_Wales_in_5_years%22_campaign_was_started_(14050400654).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Plaid Cymru rally in Machynlleth in 1949</div></div></div>\n<p>Penyberth, and Plaid Cymru\xe2\x80\x99s neutral stance during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, prompted concerns within the UK Government that it might be used by Germany to insert spies or carry out other covert operations.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In fact, the party adopted a neutral standpoint and urged (with only limited success) <a href="/wiki/Conscientious_objector" title="Conscientious objector">conscientious objection</a> to war service.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1943 Saunders Lewis contested the University of Wales parliamentary seat at a by-election, gaining 1,330 votes, or 22%. In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1945" title="United Kingdom general election, 1945">1945 general election</a>, with party membership at around 2,500, Plaid Cymru contested seven seats, as many as it had in the preceding 20 years, including constituencies in south Wales for the first time. At this time <a href="/wiki/Gwynfor_Evans" title="Gwynfor Evans">Gwynfor Evans</a> was elected president.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1950s">1950s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1950s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1959_Election_in_Merioneth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/1959_Election_in_Merioneth.jpg/220px-1959_Election_in_Merioneth.jpg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/1959_Election_in_Merioneth.jpg/330px-1959_Election_in_Merioneth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/1959_Election_in_Merioneth.jpg/440px-1959_Election_in_Merioneth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="459" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1959_Election_in_Merioneth.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1959 election in Merioneth</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC_debate_between_Iorwerth_Thomas_(Rhondda_MP)_and_Gwynfor_Evans_(15171981727).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Iorwerth Thomas and Gwynfor Evans sitting at a table in front of a BBC microphone, debating." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/BBC_debate_between_Iorwerth_Thomas_%28Rhondda_MP%29_and_Gwynfor_Evans_%2815171981727%29.jpg/220px-BBC_debate_between_Iorwerth_Thomas_%28Rhondda_MP%29_and_Gwynfor_Evans_%2815171981727%29.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/BBC_debate_between_Iorwerth_Thomas_%28Rhondda_MP%29_and_Gwynfor_Evans_%2815171981727%29.jpg/330px-BBC_debate_between_Iorwerth_Thomas_%28Rhondda_MP%29_and_Gwynfor_Evans_%2815171981727%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/BBC_debate_between_Iorwerth_Thomas_%28Rhondda_MP%29_and_Gwynfor_Evans_%2815171981727%29.jpg/440px-BBC_debate_between_Iorwerth_Thomas_%28Rhondda_MP%29_and_Gwynfor_Evans_%2815171981727%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="601" data-file-height="446" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC_debate_between_Iorwerth_Thomas_(Rhondda_MP)_and_Gwynfor_Evans_(15171981727).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>BBC debate between <a href="/wiki/Iorwerth_Thomas" title="Iorwerth Thomas">Iorwerth Thomas</a> (Rhondda MP) and <a href="/wiki/Gwynfor_Evans" title="Gwynfor Evans">Gwynfor Evans</a>, Plaid Cymru\'s first MP</div></div></div>\n<p>Gwynfor Evans\'s presidency coincided with the maturation of Plaid Cymru (as it now began to refer to itself) into a more recognisable political party. Its share of the vote increased from 0.7% in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1951" title="United Kingdom general election, 1951">1951 general election</a> to 3.1% in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1955" title="United Kingdom general election, 1955">1955</a> and 5.2% in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1955" title="United Kingdom general election, 1955">1959</a>. In the 1959 election, the party contested a majority of Welsh seats for the first time. Proposals to drown the village of <a href="/wiki/Capel_Celyn" title="Capel Celyn">Capel Celyn</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Tryweryn" class="mw-redirect" title="Tryweryn">Tryweryn</a> valley in Gwynedd in 1957 to supply the city of <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> with water played a part in Plaid Cymru\'s growth. The fact that the parliamentary bill authorising the drowning went through without support from any Welsh MPs showed that the MPs\' votes in Westminster were not enough to prevent such bills from passing.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960s">1960s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1960s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Support for the party declined slightly in the early 1960s, particularly as support for the Liberal Party began to stabilise from its long-term decline. In 1962 Saunders Lewis gave a radio talk entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Tynged_yr_Iaith" title="Tynged yr Iaith">Tynged yr Iaith</a></i> (The fate of the language) in which he predicted the extinction of the Welsh language unless action was taken. This led to the formation of <a href="/wiki/Cymdeithas_yr_Iaith_Gymraeg" class="mw-redirect" title="Cymdeithas yr Iaith Gymraeg">Cymdeithas yr Iaith Gymraeg</a> (the Welsh Language Society) the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Labour\'s return to power in 1964 and the creation of the post of <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Wales" title="Secretary of State for Wales">Secretary of State for Wales</a> appeared to represent a continuation of the incremental evolution of a distinctive Welsh polity, following the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> government\'s appointment of a Minister of Welsh Affairs in the mid-1950s and the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a> as Wales\'s capital in 1955.\n</p><p>However, in 1966, less than four months after coming in third in the constituency of <a href="/wiki/Carmarthen_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Carmarthen (UK Parliament constituency)">Carmarthen</a>, Gwynfor Evans sensationally <a href="/wiki/Carmarthen_by-election,_1966" title="Carmarthen by-election, 1966">captured</a> the seat from Labour at a by-election. This was followed by two further by-elections in <a href="/wiki/Rhondda_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Rhondda West (UK Parliament constituency)">Rhondda West</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rhondda_West_by-election,_1967" title="Rhondda West by-election, 1967">1967</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caerphilly_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Caerphilly (UK Parliament constituency)">Caerphilly</a> in 1968 in which the party achieved massive swings of 30% and 40% respectively, coming within a whisker of victory. The results were caused partly by an anti-Labour backlash. Expectations in coal mining communities that the <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Wilson</a> government would halt the long-term decline in their industry had been dashed by a significant downward revision of coal production estimates.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> However, \xe2\x80\x94 in Carmarthen particularly \xe2\x80\x94 Plaid Cymru also successfully depicted Labour\'s policies as a threat to the viability of small Welsh communities.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1970" title="United Kingdom general election, 1970">1970 general election</a> Plaid Cymru contested every seat in Wales for the first time and its vote share surged from 4.5% in 1966 to 11.5%. Gwynfor Evans lost Carmarthen to Labour, but regained the seat in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_October_1974" title="United Kingdom general election, October 1974">October 1974</a>, by which time the party had gained a further two MPs, representing the constituencies of <a href="/wiki/Caernarfon" title="Caernarfon">Caernarfon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merionethshire" title="Merionethshire">Merionethshire</a>.\n</p><p>Plaid Cymru\'s emergence (along with the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a>) prompted the Wilson government to establish the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Commission_on_the_Constitution_(United_Kingdom)" title="Royal Commission on the Constitution (United Kingdom)">Kilbrandon Commission</a> on the constitution. The subsequent proposals for a Welsh Assembly were, however, heavily defeated in a <a href="/wiki/Wales_referendum,_1979" class="mw-redirect" title="Wales referendum, 1979">referendum</a> in 1979. Despite Plaid Cymru\'s ambivalence toward home rule (as opposed to outright independence) the <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> result led many in the party to question its direction.<sup id="cite_ref-McAllister_2001_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McAllister_2001-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1979" title="United Kingdom general election, 1979">1979 general election</a> the party\'s vote share declined from 10.8% to 8.1% and Carmarthen was again lost to Labour.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Caernarfon MP <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Wigley" title="Dafydd Wigley">Dafydd Wigley</a> succeeded Gwynfor Evans as president in 1981, inheriting a party whose morale was at an all-time low. In 1981 the party adopted "community socialism" as a constitutional aim. While the party embarked on a wide-ranging review of its priorities and goals, Gwynfor Evans fought a successful campaign (including the threat of a hunger strike) to oblige the Conservative government to fulfill its promise to establish <a href="/wiki/S4C" title="S4C">S4C</a>, a Welsh-language television station.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In 1984 <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Elis-Thomas" title="Dafydd Elis-Thomas">Dafydd Elis-Thomas</a> was elected president, defeating <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Iwan" title="Dafydd Iwan">Dafydd Iwan</a>, a move that saw the party shift to the left. <a href="/wiki/Ieuan_Wyn_Jones" title="Ieuan Wyn Jones">Ieuan Wyn Jones</a> (later Plaid Cymru leader) captured <a href="/wiki/Ynys_Mon_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ynys Mon (UK Parliament constituency)">Ynys M\xc3\xb4n</a> from the Conservatives in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1987" title="United Kingdom general election, 1987">1987</a>. In 1989 Dafydd Wigley once again assumed the presidency of the party.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1992" title="United Kingdom general election, 1992">1992 general election</a> the party added a fourth MP, <a href="/wiki/Cynog_Dafis" title="Cynog Dafis">Cynog Dafis</a>, when he gained <a href="/wiki/Ceredigion_and_Pembroke_North_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceredigion and Pembroke North (UK Parliament constituency)">Ceredigion and Pembroke North</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a>. Dafis was endorsed by the local branch of the <a href="/wiki/Wales_Green_Party" title="Wales Green Party">Green Party</a>. The party\'s vote share recovered to 9.9% at the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1997" title="United Kingdom general election, 1997">1997 general election</a>.\n</p><p>In 1997, following the election of a Labour government committed to devolution for Wales, a <a href="/wiki/Welsh_devolution_referendum,_1997" title="Welsh devolution referendum, 1997">further referendum</a> was narrowly won, establishing the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a>. Plaid Cymru became the main opposition to the ruling Labour Party, with 17 seats to Labour\'s 28. In doing so, it appeared to have broken out of its rural Welsh-speaking heartland, and captured traditionally strong Labour areas in industrial <a href="/wiki/South_Wales" title="South Wales">South Wales</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plaid_Cymru_in_the_Assembly_era">Plaid Cymru in the Assembly era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Plaid Cymru in the Assembly era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span id="First_National_Assembly.2C_1999.E2.80.932003"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_National_Assembly,_1999\xe2\x80\x932003">First National Assembly, 1999\xe2\x80\x932003</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: First National Assembly, 1999\xe2\x80\x932003">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_election,_1999" title="National Assembly for Wales election, 1999">1999 election</a> Plaid Cymru gained seats in traditional Labour areas such as <a href="/wiki/Rhondda_(National_Assembly_for_Wales_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhondda (National Assembly for Wales constituency)">Rhondda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islwyn_(National_Assembly_for_Wales_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Islwyn (National Assembly for Wales constituency)">Islwyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Llanelli_(National_Assembly_for_Wales_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Llanelli (National Assembly for Wales constituency)">Llanelli</a>, achieving by far its highest share of the vote in any Wales-wide election. While Plaid Cymru regarded itself as the natural beneficiary of devolution, others attributed its performance in large part to the travails of the Labour Party<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (November 2011)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, whose nomination for <a href="/wiki/Assembly_First_Secretary" class="mw-redirect" title="Assembly First Secretary">Assembly First Secretary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Davies_(British_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ron Davies (British politician)">Ron Davies</a>, was forced to stand down in an alleged <a href="/wiki/Sex_scandal" title="Sex scandal">sex scandal</a>. The ensuing leadership battle, won by <a href="/wiki/Alun_Michael" title="Alun Michael">Alun Michael</a>, did much to damage Labour, and thus aided Plaid Cymru, whose leader was the more popular and higher profile <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Wigley" title="Dafydd Wigley">Dafydd Wigley</a>. The Labour Party\'s UK national leadership was seen to interfere in the contest and deny the popular <a href="/wiki/Rhodri_Morgan" title="Rhodri Morgan">Rhodri Morgan</a> victory.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Less than two months later, in <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_1999_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 1999 (United Kingdom)">elections to the European parliament</a>, Labour support slumped further, and Plaid Cymru came within 2.5% of achieving the largest share of the vote in Wales. Under the new system of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>, the party also gained two MEPs.\n</p><p>Plaid Cymru then developed political problems of its own. Dafydd Wigley resigned, citing health problems but amid rumours of a plot against him.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> His successor, <a href="/wiki/Ieuan_Wyn_Jones" title="Ieuan Wyn Jones">Ieuan Wyn Jones</a>, struggled to impose his authority, particularly over controversial remarks made by a councillor, Seimon Glyn.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, Labour leader and First Minister Alun Michael was replaced by Rhodri Morgan.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2001" title="United Kingdom general election, 2001">2001 general election</a>, Notwithstanding Plaid Cymru recording its highest-ever vote share in a general election, 14.3%, the party lost Wyn Jones\'s former seat of <a href="/wiki/Ynys_M%C3%B4n_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Ynys M\xc3\xb4n (UK Parliament constituency)">Ynys M\xc3\xb4n</a> to <a href="/wiki/Albert_Owen" title="Albert Owen">Albert Owen</a>, although it gained <a href="/wiki/Carmarthen_East_and_Dinefwr_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Carmarthen East and Dinefwr (UK Parliament constituency)">Carmarthen East and Dinefwr</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Adam_Price" title="Adam Price">Adam Price</a> was elected.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Second_National_Assembly.2C_2003.E2.80.9307"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_National_Assembly,_2003\xe2\x80\x9307">Second National Assembly, 2003\xe2\x80\x9307</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Second National Assembly, 2003\xe2\x80\x9307">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_election,_2003" title="National Assembly for Wales election, 2003">Assembly elections of May 2003</a> saw the party\'s representation drop from 17 to 12, with the seats gained in the 1999 election falling again to Labour and the party\'s share of the vote declining to 21%. Plaid Cymru narrowly remained the second-largest party in the National Assembly ahead of the Conservatives, Liberal Democrats and <a href="/wiki/Forward_Wales" title="Forward Wales">Forward Wales</a>.\n</p><p>On 15 September 2003 <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk-singer</a> and county councillor <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Iwan" title="Dafydd Iwan">Dafydd Iwan</a> was elected as Plaid Cymru\'s president. Ieuan Wyn Jones, who had resigned from his dual role as president and Assembly group leader following the losses in the 2003 Assembly election, was re-elected in the latter role. <a href="/wiki/Elfyn_Llwyd" title="Elfyn Llwyd">Elfyn Llwyd</a> remained the Plaid Cymru leader in the Westminster Parliament. Under Iwan\'s presidency the party formally adopted a policy of independence for Wales within Europe.\n</p><p>The 2004 local election saw the party lose control of the two South Wales councils it gained in 1999, <a href="/wiki/Rhondda_Cynon_Taff" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhondda Cynon Taff">Rhondda Cynon Taff</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caerphilly" title="Caerphilly">Caerphilly</a>, while retaining its stronghold of Gwynedd in the north-west. The results enabled the party to claim a greater number of ethnic minority councillors than all the other political parties in Wales combined,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> along with gains in authorities such as Cardiff and <a href="/wiki/Swansea" title="Swansea">Swansea</a>, where Plaid Cymru representation had been minimal. In the European Parliament elections of the same year, the party\'s vote share fell to 17.4%, and the reduction in the number of Welsh MEPs saw its representation reduced to one.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:107px;"><a href="/wiki/File:History_of_Plaid_Cymru_logo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/e4/History_of_Plaid_Cymru_logo.jpg" width="105" height="103" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="105" data-file-height="103" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:History_of_Plaid_Cymru_logo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Old logo (above) and new logo (below)</div></div></div>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2005" title="United Kingdom general election, 2005">general election</a> of 5 May 2005, Plaid Cymru lost the <a href="/wiki/Ceredigion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Ceredigion (UK Parliament constituency)">Ceredigion</a> seat to the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a>; this result was a disappointment to Plaid, who had hoped to gain <a href="/wiki/Ynys_M%C3%B4n_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Ynys M\xc3\xb4n (UK Parliament constituency)">Ynys M\xc3\xb4n</a>. Overall therefore, Plaid Cymru\'s Parliamentary representation fell to three seats, the lowest number for the party since 1992. The party\'s share of the vote fell to 12.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2006, the party voted constitutional changes to formally designate the party\'s leader in the assembly as its overall leader, with <a href="/wiki/Ieuan_Wyn_Jones" title="Ieuan Wyn Jones">Ieuan Wyn Jones</a> being restored to the full leadership and <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Iwan" title="Dafydd Iwan">Dafydd Iwan</a> becoming head of the voluntary wing<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> of the party. 2006 also saw the party unveil a radical change of image, opting to use "Plaid" as the party\'s name, although "Plaid Cymru \xe2\x80\x94 the Party of Wales" would remain the official title. The party changed its logo in 2006, from the traditional green and red <i>triban</i> (three peaks) used since 1933, to a yellow <a href="/wiki/Welsh_poppy" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh poppy">Welsh poppy</a> (<i>Meconopsis cambrica</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Third_National_Assembly.2C_2007.E2.80.9311"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_National_Assembly,_2007\xe2\x80\x9311">Third National Assembly, 2007\xe2\x80\x9311</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Third National Assembly, 2007\xe2\x80\x9311">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_election,_2007" title="National Assembly for Wales election, 2007">National Assembly election</a> of 3 May 2007, Plaid Cymru increased its number of seats from 12 to 15, regaining <a href="/wiki/Llanelli_(National_Assembly_for_Wales_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Llanelli (National Assembly for Wales constituency)">Llanelli</a>, gaining one additional list seat and winning the newly created constituency of <a href="/wiki/Aberconwy_(National_Assembly_for_Wales_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aberconwy (National Assembly for Wales constituency)">Aberconwy</a>. The 2007 election also saw Plaid Cymru\'s <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Asghar" title="Mohammad Asghar">Mohammad Asghar</a> become the first ethnic minority candidate elected to the Welsh Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The party\'s share of the vote increased to 22.4%.\n</p><p>After weeks of negotiations involving all four parties in the Assembly, Plaid Cymru and Labour agreed to form a <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition government</a>. Their agreed "<a href="/wiki/One_Wales" title="One Wales">One Wales</a>" programme included a commitment for both parties to campaign for a Yes vote in a <a href="/wiki/Welsh_devolution_referendum,_2011" title="Welsh devolution referendum, 2011">referendum on full law-making powers</a> for the Assembly, to be held at a time of the Welsh Assembly Government\'s choosing.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Ieuan Wyn Jones was subsequently confirmed as <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Wales" title="First Minister of Wales">Deputy First Minister of Wales</a><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_the_Economy_and_Transport" title="Minister for the Economy and Transport">Minister for the Economy and Transport</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rhodri_Glyn_Thomas" title="Rhodri Glyn Thomas">Rhodri Glyn Thomas</a> was appointed Heritage Minister. He later stood down, and <a href="/wiki/Alun_Ffred_Jones" title="Alun Ffred Jones">Alun Ffred Jones</a> took over. Ceredigion AM <a href="/wiki/Elin_Jones" title="Elin Jones">Elin Jones</a> was appointed to the Rural Affairs brief in the new 10-member cabinet. <a href="/wiki/Jocelyn_Davies" title="Jocelyn Davies">Jocelyn Davies</a> became Deputy Minister for Housing, and later, Regeneration.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010 general election</a>, Plaid returned three MPs to Westminster. They took part in the <a href="/wiki/Yes_for_Wales" title="Yes for Wales">Yes for Wales</a> cross-party campaign for the March 2011 referendum.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Fourth_National_Assembly.2C_2011.E2.80.9316"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Fourth_National_Assembly,_2011\xe2\x80\x9316">Fourth National Assembly, 2011\xe2\x80\x9316</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Fourth National Assembly, 2011\xe2\x80\x9316">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_election,_2011" title="National Assembly for Wales election, 2011">2011 National Assembly election</a> Plaid slipped from second place to third, being overtaken by the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Conservative_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh Conservative Party">Welsh Conservative Party</a> and losing its deputy leader <a href="/wiki/Helen_Mary_Jones" title="Helen Mary Jones">Helen Mary Jones</a>. The party held an inquiry into the election result.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The internal investigation led to the adoption of wide-ranging changes to its constitution, including a streamlining of the leadership structure.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2011, Ieuan Wyn Jones announced he would stand down as leader within the first half of the Assembly term.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> A leadership election was held in which three candidates eventually stood: <a href="/wiki/Elin_Jones" title="Elin Jones">Elin Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Elis-Thomas" title="Dafydd Elis-Thomas">Dafydd Elis-Thomas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leanne_Wood" title="Leanne Wood">Leanne Wood</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Simon_Thomas_(politician)" title="Simon Thomas (politician)">Simon Thomas</a> withdrew his candidacy before ballots were cast.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 15 March 2012, Plaid Cymru elected <a href="/wiki/Leanne_Wood" title="Leanne Wood">Leanne Wood</a> as its new leader. She received 55% of the vote, over second-placed <a href="/wiki/Elin_Jones" title="Elin Jones">Elin Jones</a> with 41%.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> She is the first female, and the first non-fluent Welsh speaker.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Soon after Wood\'s election as leader, she appointed former MP <a href="/wiki/Adam_Price" title="Adam Price">Adam Price</a> to head an economic commission for the party "focussed on bringing together tailor-made policies in order to transform our economy".<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On 1 May 2012 it was confirmed Leanne Wood would not be taking the \xc2\xa323,000 pay increase that every other party leader in the Assembly receives.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 12 November 2012, Wood announced she would be abandoning her relatively safe list seat to stand in a constituency at the 2016 National Assembly elections;<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> she later confirmed she would contest the <a href="/wiki/Rhondda_(Assembly_constituency)" title="Rhondda (Assembly constituency)">Rhondda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Adam Price was subsequently selected as the party\'s candidate for <a href="/wiki/Carmarthen_East_and_Dinefwr_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Carmarthen East and Dinefwr (UK Parliament constituency)">Carmarthen East and Dinefwr</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Lindsay Whittle confirmed he would contest the <a href="/wiki/Caerffili" class="mw-redirect" title="Caerffili">Caerffili</a> constituency.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 June 2013, former party leader <a href="/wiki/Ieuan_Wyn_Jones" title="Ieuan Wyn Jones">Ieuan Wyn Jones</a> stood down from the Assembly as the member for <a href="/wiki/Ynys_M%C3%B4n_(National_Assembly_for_Wales_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ynys M\xc3\xb4n (National Assembly for Wales constituency)">Ynys M\xc3\xb4n</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Plaid Cymru\'s candidate <a href="/wiki/Rhun_ap_Iorwerth" title="Rhun ap Iorwerth">Rhun ap Iorwerth</a> was elected as the new Assembly Member for the constituency, receiving 12,601 votes (a 58% share) with a majority of 9,166 over the Labour candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Fifth_National_Assembly.2C_2016.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Fifth_National_Assembly,_2016\xe2\x80\x93present">Fifth National Assembly, 2016\xe2\x80\x93present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fifth National Assembly, 2016\xe2\x80\x93present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_election,_2016" title="National Assembly for Wales election, 2016">2016 Welsh Assembly Elections</a>, having gained one seat Plaid Cymru became the Assembly\'s second largest party and briefly became the official opposition to the Welsh Government with 12 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Plaid Cymru currently has ten Assembly Members, following <a href="/wiki/Dafydd_Elis-Thomas" title="Dafydd Elis-Thomas">Dafydd Elis-Thomas</a>\'s resignation from the party in 2016 <sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Neil_McEvoy" title="Neil McEvoy">Neil McEvoy</a>\'s permanent expulsion from Plaid\'s Assembly group in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Helen_Mary_Jones" title="Helen Mary Jones">Helen Mary Jones</a> replaced Simon Thomas as an AM in August 2018.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">2016 referendum on the UK\'s membership of the EU</a> Plaid campaigned for a remain vote.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Wales voted 52.5% in favour of leave.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2018, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Price" title="Adam Price">Adam Price</a> ousted Leanne Wood to become Leader of Plaid Cymru following a <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru_leadership_election,_2018" title="Plaid Cymru leadership election, 2018">leadership election</a> where <a href="/wiki/Rhun_ap_Iorwerth" title="Rhun ap Iorwerth">Rhun ap Iorwerth</a> and Leanne Wood contested.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undeb_Credyd_Plaid_Cymru">Undeb Credyd Plaid Cymru</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Undeb Credyd Plaid Cymru">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Undeb Credyd Plaid Cymru Credit Union Limited is a savings and loans <a href="/wiki/Co-operative" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-operative">co-operative</a> established for party members in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Based in <a href="/wiki/Roath" title="Roath">Roath</a>, Cardiff, it is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_British_Credit_Unions" title="Association of British Credit Unions">Association of British Credit Unions</a> Limited.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Credit_union" title="Credit union">credit union</a> is authorised by the <a href="/wiki/Prudential_Regulation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Prudential Regulation Authority (United Kingdom)">Prudential Regulation Authority</a> and regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Conduct_Authority" title="Financial Conduct Authority">Financial Conduct Authority</a> and the PRA. Ultimately, like the banks and building societies, members\xe2\x80\x99 savings are protected against business failure by the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Services_Compensation_Scheme" title="Financial Services Compensation Scheme">Financial Services Compensation Scheme</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Party_leadership">Party leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" The changes in seats and votes shown for 2012 are a direct comparison since the 2008 elections in the 21 councils up for election (i.e. excluding Anglesey).\n</p><p>In 2008 Plaid won 205 seats including six in Anglesey. For the purposes of this table the 205 figure has been reduced to 199 for the 2012 elections where the party lost 41 of the 199 seats it was defending on the night, leaving them with 158 seats.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Anglesey_County_Council_election,_2013" title="Isle of Anglesey County Council election, 2013">2013 elections in Anglesey</a> the party won 12 seats, up from the 6 it won in 2008, (although significant boundary changes took place along with a reduction in the total number of seats available from 40 to 30.)\n</p><p>The 2017 figures are based on changes from the 2012 and 2013 elections.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament_elections">European Parliament elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: European Parliament elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>Percentage of<br />vote in Wales</th>\n<th>Total no.<br />of votes</th>\n<th>Seats won\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_1979_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 1979 (United Kingdom)">1979</a></td>\n<td>11.7%</td>\n<td>83,399</td>\n<td><div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">0 / 4</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; text-align: center;" class="table-no2">Opposition\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Free_Alliance">European Free Alliance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaid_Cymru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: European Free Alliance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Name <br />and Portrait\n</th>\n<th>Party Office\n</th>\n<th>Constituency <br />(if any)\n</th>\n<th>Notes\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/File:Jill_Evans.jpg" class="image" title="Jill Evans"><img alt="Jill Evans" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Jill_Evans.jpg/90px-Jill_Evans.jpg" width="90" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Jill_Evans.jpg/135px-Jill_Evans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Jill_Evans.jpg/180px-Jill_Evans.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a><br /><a href="/wiki/Jill_Evans" title="Jill Evans">Jill Evans</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/EU_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="EU Parliament">EU Parliament</a> <br />Group Leader\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Wales_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Wales (European Parliament constituency)">Wales in the EU</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Plaid retains close links with the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> (SNP), with both parties\' MPs co-operating closely with one another. They work as a single parliamentary group within <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Westminster</a>, and were involved in joint campaigning during the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2005" title="United Kingdom general election, 2005">2005 general election</a> campaign. Both Plaid and the SNP, along with <a href="/wiki/Mebyon_Kernow" title="Mebyon Kernow">Mebyon Kernow</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> are members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Alliance" title="European Free Alliance">European Free Alliance</a> (EFA), a pan-<a href="/wiki/European_political_party" title="European political party">European political party</a> for <a href="/wiki/Regionalism_(politics)" title="Regionalism (politics)">regionalist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autonomism_(political_doctrine)" title="Autonomism (political doctrine)">autonomist</a> and pro-independence political parties across Europe. The EFA co-operates with the larger <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Party" title="European Green Party">European Green Party</a> to form <a href="/wiki/The_Greens%E2%80%93European_Free_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="The Greens\xe2\x80\x93European Free Alliance">The Greens\xe2\x80\x93European Free Alliance</a> (Greens/EFA) <a href="/wiki/Political_groups_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Political groups of the European Parliament">political group</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span
